  Only the Qwen LLM goes to GPU. Embedder + reranker are small (50M / ~300M
  params) and run fine on CPU, so they stay with the orchestrator вҖ” that keeps
  the seam to a single clean boundary. To flip the switch you change one env var
  on the CPU server. Both LLM consumers (SAM reasoner + ingestion extractor)
  follow it automatically.

  The real engineering work is on the GPU side: serving the model on Lightning 
  persistently, securely, and reachable from the CPU box (Lightning Studios
  sleep when idle, and Ollama has no built-in auth).

вҸә That settles it. Here's my plan and I'll start executing the parts I can do
  locally right now.

  Connectivity recommendation: Cloudflare Tunnel from the Lightning Studio.
  Reasoning вҖ” Lightning Studios sleep and get new IPs each session, so the CPU
  box needs a stable target; cloudflared runs purely outbound (no TUN device,
  which Lightning's containers don't give you), gives you a fixed hostname like
  gpu.akhrots.com, and adds free TLS + token auth вҖ” which solves the fact that
  Ollama itself has no auth. (Tailscale is the fallback if you'd rather not put
  a hostname on Cloudflare DNS.)

  One cost reality to flag up front: the whole point was to stop paying for 24/7
  GPU. A Lightning Studio also sleeps when idle вҖ” so the robust design is
  graceful degradation: SAM already has a HeuristicConflictResolver fallback
  when the LLM is unreachable, so reads still work (degraded) while the GPU is
  cold, and a wake call spins it back up. We'll lean on that rather than burning
  GPU hours around the clock.

  Before I generate the Ollama serving bundle, I need to match exactly how
  gml-qwen-ft was built in production (chat template, system prompt, sampling
  params вҖ” these matter for the FT model to behave correctly). Let me find the
  existing Modelfile / creation script in the snapshot.

  3. Elastic IP вҖ” important reality check first

  Here's the catch with "keep 54.197.40.255 constant": that address is an
  auto-assigned (ephemeral) IP, and AWS cannot convert an existing ephemeral IP 
  into a permanent one in place. An Elastic IP will be a new, different number
  that then never changes. So "make it permanent" unavoidably means a one-time 
  switch to a new IP + updating Hostinger DNS to that new number.

  You said "set up the elastic IP," so I'll proceed on that path. Run this in
  CloudShell вҖ” it allocates, associates, and prints your new permanent IP:

  ALLOC=$(aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc --region us-east-1 --query
  AllocationId --output text)
  aws ec2 associate-address --instance-id i-0fdef601709d34ac1 --allocation-id
  $ALLOC --region us-east-1
  echo "NEW PERMANENT IP:"; aws ec2 describe-addresses --allocation-ids $ALLOC
  --region us-east-1 --query "Addresses[0].PublicIp" --output text

  вҡ пёҸ The moment it associates, 54.197.40.255 stops working and the site is dark
  until you repoint DNS. So:
  1. Run the above вҶ’ paste me the NEW IP.
  2. Update Hostinger DNS (apex @ and www) to the new IP.
  3. I'll re-verify HTTPS + reissue/confirm the cert on the new IP and update my
  SSH config вҖ” the cert is domain-based so it stays valid.

  Or, if you'd rather not change the IP again right now: leave it as-is and
  simply never stop/start the instance (a reboot keeps the IP; only stopвҶ’start
  changes it). Tell me which вҖ” paste the new IP to go permanent, or say "leave
  it" and I'll move back to finishing the GML backend.

  рҹ”ҙ Flaws found

  CRITICAL вҖ” already fixed during review (the backend couldn't run without 
  these):
  1. Stale schema вҖ” vm-bootstrap applies all_in_one.sql, which is frozen at
  ~migrationВ 009. The deployed code needs columns/tables from 010вҖ“016
  (entity_id, is_latest, session_id, bitemporal, entities, etc.). Health
  endpoint 500'd. Fixed: rebuilt schema from numbered migrations 001вҶ’016.
  2. Migration 012 bug вҖ” 012_invite_codes.sql inserts into
  schema_migrations(version) but the column is filename (013 does it right).
  This breaks both the raw path and apply_all.sh. Production only worked because
  it deployed via all_in_one. Fixed at source (server + recovered repo).

  HIGH вҖ” feature gaps (expected from the partial deploy, but real):
  3. LLM flows down вҖ” chat вҶ’ 500 (Ollama: All connection attempts failed), LLM
  ingest вҶ’ 503. Root cause: GML_OLLAMA_BASE_URL=localhost (no LLM on EC2) and
  --no-sam disabled the LLM path. Needs the CPUвҶ’GPU link wired + SAM LLM
  enabled.
  4. Not using the fine-tuned models вҖ” running generic fastembed:bge-small +
  jina reranker, not embedder_locomo_ft / ce_locomo_ft. Recall quality is
  vanilla baseline. Needs FT models uploaded + st backend.
  5. MCP server not running вҖ” bootstrap only created gml-api; gml-mcp (:8765) is
  down, so the MCP flow is unavailable.

  MEDIUM вҖ” genuine bugs:
  6. ID inconsistency вҖ” POST /api/memories returns id: manual-<uuid>
  (api_routes.py:537) but persists as conv-<вҖҰ>; the returned id 404s on 
  GET/DELETE. Clients can't act on the response id.
  7. Chat hard-fails when the LLM is unreachable (500) instead of degrading to
  returning memories.

  LOW вҖ” polish:
  8. Inconsistent request fields: recall uses query, but trace/chat use text.
  9. SDP regex ingest missed a plausible fact ("adopted a dog named Pixel" вҶ’ 0
  extracted).
  10. GML_OLLAMA_MODEL=qwen2.5:3b placeholder (should be gml-qwen-ft).

  Prioritized fix plan

  1. Wire CPUвҶ’GPU (Tailscale EC2вҶ”Lightning), set GML_OLLAMA_BASE_URLвҶ’GPU,
  GML_OLLAMA_MODEL=gml-qwen-ft, drop --no-sam-llm вҶ’ fixes #3, #7, #10 and
  unlocks chat + LLM ingest.
  2. Upload FT models + switch to st backend вҶ’ fixes #4.
  3. Stand up gml-mcp service вҶ’ fixes #5.
  4. Code fix for #6 (return persisted id) + normalize field names #8.
  5. Regenerate all_in_one.sql from 001вҶ’016 so future deploys aren't broken
  (#1/#2 permanent fix).

  Two notes: I left test data under throwaway users (reviewer/intruder/t@t.com)
  вҖ” I can purge it. And the GPU upload (fp16/merged still pending, ~2 h) doesn't
  block any of the above since the model already serves via Q5.

  Want me to proceed with the fix plan вҖ” starting with #1 (the GPU link, which
  unblocks the most)?

  Yes, I'm certain the chat/ingest failures are NOT related to the pending

  - The chat error was Ollama: All connection attempts failed вҖ” a network error
  (EC2 dialing localhost:11434 where nothing's running). The ingest 503 was
  MemoryExtractor not initialized вҖ” a config flag (--no-sam turned the LLM path
  off). Neither is a model error.
  - The Qwen model is already fully serving on the GPU from the Q5_K_M GGUF вҖ” we
  tested it ("Paris", 0.65s). The files still uploading (Q8_0, fp16, merged,
  adapter) are just alternate formats of the same model вҖ” pure
  redundancy/flexibility, not needed for anything to work.
  - The only model-related flaw is #4 (generic embedder instead of
  embedder_locomo_ft/ce_locomo_ft) вҖ” and those are CPU-side models I haven't
  pushed to EC2 yet; they affect recall quality, not whether chat works.

  So wiring the network link will make chat/ingest work right now, with the Q5
  model that's already up. Let me build the link.

  The relay (how I beat Lightning's 1 MB/s cap)

  Direct push to the studio is capped at ~1 MB/s by Lightning's SSH gateway (вҶ’
  ~4 h). Instead: MacвҶ’EC2 (6 MB/s) вҶ’ studio pulls from EC2 over a private SSH 
  forward (27 MB/s). The studio-side pull is ~10 min and overlaps. Net ~45 min
  vs 4 hours. The push is private (no public webroot вҖ” that got correctly
  blocked earlier).

  Auto-sequence once the pieces land

  1. torch done вҶ’ switch GML to GML_EMBEDDER=st + FT reranker ensemble вҶ’
  best-quality retrieval (this lands in ~5 min, independent of the big upload).
  2. Relay done вҶ’ studio pulls the formats, I register fp16 as gml-qwen-ft вҶ’
  best-quality LLM serving.
  3. Re-test recall/ingest to confirm the uncompromised stack.

  Already done this session (recap)

  - вң… akhrots.com live over HTTPS
  - вң… GML backend healthy (schema bugs fixed, RLS isolation verified)
  - вң… CPUвҶ’GPU link (LLM ingest extracting facts via GPU)
  - вң… FT retrieval models already copied to EC2

  I'll continue automatically as each completes and report. The /chat token-cap
  fix is still queued after the quality upgrades.

вҸә Server and DNS are both globally fine вҖ” all three public resolvers
  (Google/Cloudflare/Quad9) return 54.197.40.255, and /app serves correctly
  (HTTP 200, "Akhrot вҖ” Memory", 0.7 s). So this is local to your desktop, not
  the deployment.

  Since mobile (cellular = fresh resolver) works but desktop doesn't, it's
  almost certainly your desktop's DNS cache or browser cache still holding the
  old parked IP (136.113.88.125, which times out). Quick fixes, in order:

  1. Incognito/private window вҶ’ https://akhrots.com/app (bypasses browser cache
  + HSTS). Fastest test.
  2. Flush DNS on the desktop:
    - macOS: sudo dscacheutil -flushcache; sudo killall -HUP mDNSResponder
    - Windows: ipconfig /flushdns
  3. Hard refresh: Cmd/Ctrl + Shift + R.
  4. Try a different browser or your phone on Wi-Fi (same network as desktop вҖ”
  if that also fails, it's your router/ISP resolver caching, and flushing the
  router or switching the desktop to 1.1.1.1/8.8.8.8 DNS fixes it).

  To pin it down exactly вҖ” what does the desktop actually show?
  - "This site can't be reached" / timeout / "server not found" вҶ’ DNS (desktop
  still on old IP) вҶ’ flush DNS
  - The old parked/blank page or marketing-only вҶ’ cache вҶ’ incognito
  - A white/blank page that loads but shows nothing вҶ’ that'd be an app/JS issue
  and I'd dig into that instead

  Tell me which one you see and I'll nail it.
